  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_33f8fdde-2daa-4e22-9701-21c545e561d7'

  <span id="freeText15698826386333513369" style="display:none">For more than twenty years Natalie Goldberg has been challenging and cheering on writers with her books and workshops. In her groundbreaking first book, she brings together Zen meditation and writing in a new way. Writing practice, as she calls it, is no different from other forms of Zen practice--"it is backed by two thousand years of studying the mind." This edition includes a new preface and an interview with the author.</span>

<div id="review_114202397" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/114202397" />
    <a title="Jason Koivu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu"><img alt="Jason Koivu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560521450p2/1742824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/114202397?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Koivu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Koivu" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu">Jason Koivu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=writing">writing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114202397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15180917021249842981">Natalie Goldberg's droning voice sapped the life out of anything of value she had to say. And what did she have to say? Pretty much the same as other how-to-write books. <br/><br/><i>Writing Down the Bones</i> is your bog-standard cheerleader-style writing advice, but delivered in a cheerless voice: g.o...y.o.u...you can do it.... That sort of stuff can be inspiring when done right, but a whole book's worth will take the punch out of any pep talk. <br/><br/>Clearly it was a mistake to listen to Goldberg narrate this one o</span>
  <span id="freeText15180917021249842981" style="display:none">Natalie Goldberg's droning voice sapped the life out of anything of value she had to say. And what did she have to say? Pretty much the same as other how-to-write books. <br><br><i>Writing Down the Bones</i> is your bog-standard cheerleader-style writing advice, but delivered in a cheerless voice: g.o...y.o.u...you can do it.... That sort of stuff can be inspiring when done right, but a whole book's worth will take the punch out of any pep talk. <br><br>Clearly it was a mistake to listen to Goldberg narrate this one on tape. Yeah, I listened to this on cassette. Hey, I had an old car with a cassette deck and 30 minutes to and from work to kill. Roadrage can be quelled with a good audiobook. Unfortunately. <i>Writing Down the Bones</i> made me want to play pinball with my Hyundai, using the other cars on the highway as the bumpers. <br><br>Frankly I found a great deal more worth in Stephen King's <i>On Writing</i> and I'm not even a big King fan. <i>Writing Down the Bones</i> won't steer you wrong, hell you might even learn a thing or two, but it nearly had me steering for the nearest bridge abutment.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1410200740i/11073447.jpg" width="200" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="15180917021249842981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1225537-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535727274p2/1225537.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/28243107?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/1225537-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Young or beginning writers who don't mind hearing a spiritual dimension added to writing</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Michelle by: </span>
      Professor Robert Bensen
  </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer28243107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10475906893064750497">I've owned this book for six years. My copy is the pocket-size version. Its cover is wrapped in packing tape to slow the dog-earing.<br/><br/>The first time I read this book in college, and many times since, I carried it everywhere with me, reading it before classes, and over lunch in the dining hall. Natalie Goldberg's short, friendly chapters filled with spiritual and practical wisdom and stories made me feel as though a very warm and welcoming teacher had sat down across the table from me and struck up</span>
  <span id="freeText10475906893064750497" style="display:none">I've owned this book for six years. My copy is the pocket-size version. Its cover is wrapped in packing tape to slow the dog-earing.<br /><br />The first time I read this book in college, and many times since, I carried it everywhere with me, reading it before classes, and over lunch in the dining hall. Natalie Goldberg's short, friendly chapters filled with spiritual and practical wisdom and stories made me feel as though a very warm and welcoming teacher had sat down across the table from me and struck up a conversation about writing and the writing life.<br /><br />I have read some criticisms of this book, and all I can say is that for me, it works. If you are looking for a book of writing exercises, instructions on prosody or advice on how to revise, this isn't that book. If you don't want to hear about Zen Buddhism, this book is not for you. <br /><br />What this book does for me is make me want to write again. It is very much comfort reading, something I can carry around in my purse, pull out at a bus stop and read any chapter, then look out at the world with eyes a little more open and a mind a little more clear. And most importantly, it makes me want to write.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10475906893064750497" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_129179792" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129179792" />
    <a title="Gabriel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/101529-gabriel"><img alt="Gabriel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1180845769p2/101529.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129179792?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabriel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabriel" href="/user/show/101529-gabriel">Gabriel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129179792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9737300842620993251">For you poets out there, this book is for you.<br/><br/>For those of you meant to write memoirs and light happy stories about light happy things, this book is for you.<br/><br/>For those of you who want to write about things of no consequence that have some consequence - The Light Coming Through The Window, Your Favorite Meal, Blue - this book is for you too.<br/><br/>For those of us who are busy thinking of short stories, who are thinking of horror, who think of sf that may deal with harder topics, that think of things that</span>
  <span id="freeText9737300842620993251" style="display:none">For you poets out there, this book is for you.<br /><br />For those of you meant to write memoirs and light happy stories about light happy things, this book is for you.<br /><br />For those of you who want to write about things of no consequence that have some consequence - The Light Coming Through The Window, Your Favorite Meal, Blue - this book is for you too.<br /><br />For those of us who are busy thinking of short stories, who are thinking of horror, who think of sf that may deal with harder topics, that think of things that may not be so happy and want to write those things down. For those of us who are dedicated to our short stories and don't want to think in poetical terms (unless, of course, you are an Artiste!), this book does not have as much for us as I had wished.<br /><br />It's not for lack of trying. Indeed, the thrust of this book is to free the idea of what it means to write. Stuck in a section? Why don't you try dressing up as someone else and move to a different location and write there! Sentences too boring? Why don't you change word order and play with that punctuation! <br /><br />And yet, for each one of these things that it brings up, I felt less and less like Natalie Goldberg was talking to me and more like she was talking to the Poet across town. She speaks in a language meant for the Burl Ives of this world. And, you know, kudos to them! We need those folk just as much as we need the David Lynches. But I hoped for a little more. I wanted something that forced me to write. Because (and this is why I was "reading" this book for the last 9 months) I wrote for 10 minutes after each chapter. I wanted something that would gear my writing and yet, for 90% of those writings, I was just meandering about a phrase that I wanted to argue about or some other thing. <br /><br />I'm sure there are many out there who want to read this book, and if you fall into one of those lists from the start, you will get TONS from this book. Otherwise, maybe read [Book: Bird By Bird: Some Instructions on Writing and Life] by Anne Lamott instead?</span>
  <a data-text-id="9737300842620993251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_30155259" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/30155259" />
    <a title="Bonnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1424859-bonnie"><img alt="Bonnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1229215019p2/1424859.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/30155259?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie" href="/user/show/1424859-bonnie">Bonnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780877733751" href="/book/show/578518.Writing_Down_the_Bones">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1424859-bonnie?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1424859-bonnie?shelf=on-writing">on-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1424859-bonnie?shelf=reviewed-books">reviewed-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer30155259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14140461094776871168">I picked up Writing Down the Bones when I was still teaching elementary school, and used ideas from it with my grades two to four students. My emphasis on these “10-minute writes” was on unedited (until later) free-writing. The rules were a condensed version of Natalie’s: <br/>-Keep your hand moving<br/>-Don’t cross out<br/>-Don’t worry about spelling, punctuation, grammar<br/>-Don’t think<br/><br/>I would set the timer, and on the word, “start”, pencils began moving, some faster than others. And of course I would be writing</span>
  <span id="freeText14140461094776871168" style="display:none">I picked up Writing Down the Bones when I was still teaching elementary school, and used ideas from it with my grades two to four students. My emphasis on these “10-minute writes” was on unedited (until later) free-writing. The rules were a condensed version of Natalie’s: <br />-Keep your hand moving<br />-Don’t cross out<br />-Don’t worry about spelling, punctuation, grammar<br />-Don’t think<br /><br />I would set the timer, and on the word, “start”, pencils began moving, some faster than others. And of course I would be writing, too. Some students had no difficulty; others couldn’t let go. No matter; it wasn’t a competition. When the timer went off, I’d say, “Pencils down”, and pages were filed into their writing folders. <br /><br />After doing a number of these exercises, when a student thought there might be a story to develop, the raw material of the “stream-of-consciousness” draft was used to expand on the idea, rewrite, and then edit. Eventually, each student improved in fluency and was able to create a “hard-cover” book. Some stories contained a line per page with an illustration. Others filled their book with writing, and the odd illustration. The “published” copy contained a picture of the author on the back, along with a short bio. <br /><br />Quite a number of years later, I participated in a workshop facilitated by a friend and fan of Natalie Goldberg. Most of the exercises began with the words, “I remember….”<br /><br />To this day I still use a pen and paper, instead of the computer, to begin a new chapter or scene, or if I get ‘stuck’ in the middle of one. <br /><br />I would recommend this book for all writers, but especially for beginning writers. And for teachers who might want to incorporate this exercise into their writing curriculum. As the title suggests, “Writing Down the Bones” is actually “Freeing the writer within.” This is a book, not about the revision required for all “published” writing, but about generating and recording the essential ideas in the first place. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14140461094776871168" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_21415271" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21415271" />
    <a title="Jenny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1113490-jenny"><img alt="Jenny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1367090180p2/1113490.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21415271?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny" href="/user/show/1113490-jenny">Jenny</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113490-jenny?shelf=writing">writing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21415271" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2119460099189006686">This is a great starting-point aspiring-writer's book, terrific for getting the creative juices flowing. I have used Natalie Goldberg's techniques both as a writer and as a writing teacher. Eventually, if you want to write Things That Other People Want to Read and not just Things That Are Good to Write, you need to work on the less free-spirited, less blue-sky, and occasionally less exciting stuff: structure, pacing, whittling away extraneous words. You need to learn to *re*write, to do somethin</span>
  <span id="freeText2119460099189006686" style="display:none">This is a great starting-point aspiring-writer's book, terrific for getting the creative juices flowing. I have used Natalie Goldberg's techniques both as a writer and as a writing teacher. Eventually, if you want to write Things That Other People Want to Read and not just Things That Are Good to Write, you need to work on the less free-spirited, less blue-sky, and occasionally less exciting stuff: structure, pacing, whittling away extraneous words. You need to learn to *re*write, to do something with the "bones" you've flung onto the page. This book won't take you there, but it opens up the first important part of the writing process, of accessing imagination and getting words on the page. <br /><br />It's worth mentioning that Goldberg uses writing as a Zen Buddhist practice, like meditation, and in that context it's the writing itself, not the end product, that is important anyway.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2119460099189006686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_37447090" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37447090" />
    <a title="Nicky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/223837-nicky"><img alt="Nicky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308224598p2/223837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/37447090?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicky" href="/user/show/223837-nicky">Nicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780877733751" href="/book/show/578518.Writing_Down_the_Bones">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=about-writing">about-writing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer37447090" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1834670448384317115">Reading Writing Down The Bones by Natalie Goldberg and Bird by Bird by Anne Lamott struck me as reading two very similar books from two distinct voices. Writing Down The Bones is a personal reflection on the craft and what works for Goldberg and might work for you. It's easy to digest, coming in short chapters, and it really does make you think about what you write, how you sit down to work, whether you're really dedicated to writing. The allusions to Buddhism and Judaism and how they affect her</span>
  <span id="freeText1834670448384317115" style="display:none">Reading Writing Down The Bones by Natalie Goldberg and Bird by Bird by Anne Lamott struck me as reading two very similar books from two distinct voices. Writing Down The Bones is a personal reflection on the craft and what works for Goldberg and might work for you. It's easy to digest, coming in short chapters, and it really does make you think about what you write, how you sit down to work, whether you're really dedicated to writing. The allusions to Buddhism and Judaism and how they affect her writing are also interesting. Some of her advice seems contradictory, but really it's just that it comes from different places in the process. Some of it is the average advice you get from all writers -- keep a notebook, take it everywhere, write in it every day, just as an example -- but coupled with her experience of doing that.<br /><br />I felt like it was a little bit repetitive and it didn't focus much on what to do with the writing once you've done it, but it was still worth reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1834670448384317115" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who wants to improve their writing skills, or understanding of the writing process</span></div>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Laurie by: </span>
      Dr. Michael Angelotti
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1431048-laurie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer31621321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18003917831623138518">This book changed my life as a writer, a teacher of writing, and as an individual!<br/><br/>I use this book currently in my high school Creative Writing I class. I read chapters to the students; we talk about what they might mean, and how the advice given could change their writing. I wasn't sure if this approach would be successful with high school age students, but within weeks I have seen more free writing, more stream of consciousness writing, and more unedited writing than ever before! My students ar</span>
  <span id="freeText18003917831623138518" style="display:none">This book changed my life as a writer, a teacher of writing, and as an individual!<br /><br />I use this book currently in my high school Creative Writing I class. I read chapters to the students; we talk about what they might mean, and how the advice given could change their writing. I wasn't sure if this approach would be successful with high school age students, but within weeks I have seen more free writing, more stream of consciousness writing, and more unedited writing than ever before! My students are enjoying the drafting and brainstorming stages of writing because they seem to be less intimidating. If they don't know what to write, they free write until an idea comes to mind! <br /><br />Thanks Natalie!<br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2047670263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5665245607980046590">This is an encouraging and motivating little volume, filled with an assortment of anecdotes, advice, and exercises for writing practice; it is a good way to get into the habit of writing. It has, however, one of the ugliest book covers I have ever seen. <br/><br/><i>Writing Down the Bones</i> promotes a Zen-like writing practice, in which no errors are possible, provided that one be present and continue to write. Goldberg gives the student permission to write badly, and creates a liberating safe-space that helps</span>
  <span id="freeText5665245607980046590" style="display:none">This is an encouraging and motivating little volume, filled with an assortment of anecdotes, advice, and exercises for writing practice; it is a good way to get into the habit of writing. It has, however, one of the ugliest book covers I have ever seen. <br /><br /><i>Writing Down the Bones</i> promotes a Zen-like writing practice, in which no errors are possible, provided that one be present and continue to write. Goldberg gives the student permission to write badly, and creates a liberating safe-space that helps a lot of students find the courage to write, and eventually to discover that they have something valuable within them. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5665245607980046590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText9454763295481769971" style="display:none">I put it under inspirational, since it does have a lot of that, but this is also the best writing book I have read. I got it on the recommendation of a colleague of mine when I was still teaching high school English. It has inspired me to be a better writer myself. And it is just a good book to read when you need something that is easy and relaxing. Goldberg is very encouraging, inspiring, and gentle with a bit of an erotic element. I am finally adding it now as I am rereading it yet again. True, it was written before computers really took off, but I am sure a lot of the advice is still very applicable. For instance, I am sure instead of notebooks and diners, you may be using a laptop in a coffee shop with wifi. Overall, the book remains very effective and timeless. </span>

<div id="review_183708113" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183708113" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/183708113?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne Ku" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne Ku" href="/user/show/1246726-anne-ku">Anne Ku</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer183708113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6600475472195534663">I went to a Writing Group in the Hague today for the first time. Seeing the half-read paperback "Writing Down the Bones" on someone's table made me curious as I had heard of it before. <br/><br/>I simply couldn't put it down.<br/><br/>So I negotiated with the owner of the book, the friend who introduced me to the writing group, to swap the book I was reading (something about taking back your life, another self-help book I was half-way through and wanted to finish and give away because there were too many of such bo</span>
  <span id="freeText6600475472195534663" style="display:none">I went to a Writing Group in the Hague today for the first time. Seeing the half-read paperback "Writing Down the Bones" on someone's table made me curious as I had heard of it before. <br /><br />I simply couldn't put it down.<br /><br />So I negotiated with the owner of the book, the friend who introduced me to the writing group, to swap the book I was reading (something about taking back your life, another self-help book I was half-way through and wanted to finish and give away because there were too many of such books on my shelf and repertoire) -- for her book to finish reading by tomorrow.<br /><br />I read Goldberg's bestseller on the steps next to the famous Dr Anton Philipzaal (concert hall) after a much-needed salt-and-pepper squid and rice take-out meal. I continued reading it on the train back to Utrecht, hoping the train ride would not end.<br /><br />As soon as I got home, I sat in the garden in the setting northern European sun, anxious to digest the remaining pearls of wisdom before the sun disappeared from the roof tops of the monument houses.<br /><br />I finished the book in less than a day.<br /><br />I guess I was desperate. <br /><br />I had not read a book about writing in a long time. I had loads to write, but I could not even do the "free writing" of today's writing session, only jotting down bullet points and ideas from my head, flushing out the burden of responsibility to write reviews and more. I had not kept a journal for more than a year. I was stuck.<br /><br />Reading Natalie Goldberg's book freed the writer within me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6600475472195534663" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_91793053" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/91793053" />
    <a title="Tim Dudek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3264054-tim-dudek"><img alt="Tim Dudek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337284651p2/3264054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/91793053?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim Dudek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim Dudek" href="/user/show/3264054-tim-dudek">Tim Dudek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91793053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17886191781631368312">Having heard great praise for this book from several people I respect I had high hopes. Like many, I found it lacking. Golberg wrote a book not about writing but about using Zen to overcoming self doubt. I am sure this could be quite helpful to many prospective writers. Judging by the many positive reviews this is the case. And to those of you I say, “More power to ya”. I rarely wallow in self doubt of my writing ability. I fail to write not because I am afraid, but because I am lazy and easily </span>
  <span id="freeText17886191781631368312" style="display:none">Having heard great praise for this book from several people I respect I had high hopes. Like many, I found it lacking. Golberg wrote a book not about writing but about using Zen to overcoming self doubt. I am sure this could be quite helpful to many prospective writers. Judging by the many positive reviews this is the case. And to those of you I say, “More power to ya”. I rarely wallow in self doubt of my writing ability. I fail to write not because I am afraid, but because I am lazy and easily distracted. <br />Natalie Goldberg spends most of the short chapters in this short book talking about her Zen teacher and about embracing irrationality. Maybe this technique helps poets but it seems unhelpful to prose writers. She highlights this in one chapter where she lists several poems. They are a gibberish and incoherent jumble of unconnected words. <br />I did glean two actual pieces of practical advice from this fifteen dollar book. First, write a lot. This should not shock anyone since this every book, article, and seminar about writing contains the same advice. I found the second idea far more helpful. We need to separate the writer in us from the editor. Put simply, don’t edit your work as you are writing. Just get the words on the page. Don’t like something in that sentence? Ignore it and just keep writing. Come back later and edit it. <br />There I’ve given you the two things you will actually get from this book and just saved you fifteen dollars. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17886191781631368312" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9462859875082434546">It took my ego 15 years to crack open Stephen King's memoir, On Writing. When I finally did, I was transformed. . . how could his writing process be so similar to mine? Why do he and I have the same strange thoughts? <br/><br/>The deep connection to that book led me to rethink this book, Writing Down the Bones, that has sat, barely touched, upon my night stand for nearly a decade.<br/><br/>I have come to realize, through these two excellent books, that it's good to journey outside of your powerfully resistant ego a</span>
  <span id="freeText9462859875082434546" style="display:none">It took my ego 15 years to crack open Stephen King's memoir, On Writing. When I finally did, I was transformed. . . how could his writing process be so similar to mine? Why do he and I have the same strange thoughts? <br /><br />The deep connection to that book led me to rethink this book, Writing Down the Bones, that has sat, barely touched, upon my night stand for nearly a decade.<br /><br />I have come to realize, through these two excellent books, that it's good to journey outside of your powerfully resistant ego and your own short-sightedness when it comes to seeking help. It's not even about "help." Natalie Goldberg wants you to remember that, if you are provoked to write, it's for a reason, and the only way to set yourself free is to validate your expression by working at it, daily.<br /><br />Whether you're a veteran or a novice, you need this book.</span>

  <span id="freeText10716510710361972167" style="display:none">I love, love, love this book with all of my beating heart. <br /><br />There's a kind of fuzzy warmth, like standing present on a balcony overlooking autumnal woods and hearing the sounds of bird songs, as I finished Writing Down the Bones. <br /><br />I want to tape this book to my chest and keep it with me always. <div id="review_1717277993" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1717277993" />
    <a title="Bill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18983476-bill"><img alt="Bill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595589280p2/18983476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1717277993?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bill" href="/user/show/18983476-bill">Bill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1717277993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11686566406573436720"><b>3.5 STARS</b><br/><br/>Back in September I joined the newly formed Westfield Writer's Project <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.facebook.com/groups/1164140453664143/'>https://www.facebook.com/groups/11641...</a> and one of our writing assignments was to read a book on the craft of writing and and share our thoughts at our next meeting. I chose Writing Down The Bones!<br/><br/>Perhaps it was the curious title that included the words “bones” and “writing” that attracted me to this book. Or maybe because it came up so many times during my messaging conversations with the WWP moderator over several</span>
  <span id="freeText11686566406573436720" style="display:none"><b>3.5 STARS</b><br /><br />Back in September I joined the newly formed Westfield Writer's Project <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/groups/1164140453664143/">https://www.facebook.com/groups/11641...</a> and one of our writing assignments was to read a book on the craft of writing and and share our thoughts at our next meeting. I chose Writing Down The Bones!<br /><br />Perhaps it was the curious title that included the words “bones” and “writing” that attracted me to this book. Or maybe because it came up so many times during my messaging conversations with the WWP moderator over several months that the seeds of familiarity sprouted and took root in my head. Regardless of how I got here, I am so pleased to read this wonderful primer on the craft of writing.<br /><br />The idea of just digging in without goals or expectations of the next great America novel resonated with me as refreshing and truly liberating. Invariably I’ve approached my writing with lofty and unrealistic expectations of a perfectly polished product each and every time I sat down to write. And because I never could achieve those pie in the sky expectations, writing often felt like a frustrating chore wrought with failure. Goldberg has set me free! Beginner’s mind and mindfulness, staying in the moment without expectations or fear, are elements of my yoga practice that I never thought to apply to writing.<br /><br />Goldberg suggests we approach writing as a practice. Like long distance running, playing the piano or baking pastries, the more we do it, the better we get at it. But the practice must be consistent and scheduled regardless of how we feel or the level of motivation. As Nike proclaims, just do it! When we practice, Goldberg suggests, sit with no expectations of yourself. You are free to write the worst junk in the world!<br /><br />I'm loving the writer's group, loved this book and love writing the junk!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11686566406573436720" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6006948591479256510">I tried to read this book many, many years ago and quit because I didn't get much out of it. There were occasional insights, but not nearly enough meat to keep me going. It is still on all the "must read" lists for writers, so I thought I'd give it another chance. After all, I was a teenager the last time I tried and I didn't have a lot of patience for things I didn't understand.<br/><br/>I should have trusted my teen self. <br/><br/>I was able to hit upon a few nuggets of wisdom, but for the most part, I was readi</span>
  <span id="freeText6006948591479256510" style="display:none">I tried to read this book many, many years ago and quit because I didn't get much out of it. There were occasional insights, but not nearly enough meat to keep me going. It is still on all the "must read" lists for writers, so I thought I'd give it another chance. After all, I was a teenager the last time I tried and I didn't have a lot of patience for things I didn't understand.<br /><br />I should have trusted my teen self. <br /><br />I was able to hit upon a few nuggets of wisdom, but for the most part, I was reading words -- just reading a series of words that held no interest or importance for me. I didn't find those words to be especially informative, nor did I find them to be especially inspiring. <br /><br />Maybe if I wait another 35 years to read the book, I'll finally understand what all the hype is about.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_183935107" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183935107" />
    <a title="Cassandra Hawkins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4575864-cassandra-hawkins"><img alt="Cassandra Hawkins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587186532p2/4575864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/183935107?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cassandra Hawkins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cassandra Hawkins" href="/user/show/4575864-cassandra-hawkins">Cassandra Hawkins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer183935107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9728018122052966406">Yesterday, I finished "Writing Down the Bones: Freeing the Writer Within," by Natalie Goldberg. I started reading this book years ago. I began this book, when I was attending the University of Mississippi Writing Project Summer Institute. This Summer Institute was designed to teach teachers how to write and teach writing. At that time, I was only a special education teacher with a Master's degree in English, yearning and longing to teach English. Who would have thought that years later I would f</span>
  <span id="freeText9728018122052966406" style="display:none">Yesterday, I finished "Writing Down the Bones: Freeing the Writer Within," by Natalie Goldberg. I started reading this book years ago. I began this book, when I was attending the University of Mississippi Writing Project Summer Institute. This Summer Institute was designed to teach teachers how to write and teach writing. At that time, I was only a special education teacher with a Master's degree in English, yearning and longing to teach English. Who would have thought that years later I would finish this book and use it in my English class on the collegiate level?<br /><br /><br />This book is really great. What I like about this book is that you are taken away from the constraints of "normal" writing. You are encouraged to write. Goldberg's writing tips are beyond the realms of what is considered to be the normal method of teaching writing. Of course, I love her for this fact. Perhaps, I love her because I am different...hmmmm. Ok, I need to focus on the book.<br /><br /><br />Today, I used one of the writing techniques from the book. I did a writing marathon with my students at Jackson State University. I put my students in a circle and put topics in a basket. I had a student pulled topics out of the basket. Students have a choice to write on the topic or write what's on their mind.The session is timed. I did four sessions of 10 minutes. After the first 10 minutes of non-stop writing. Students read their work. No one comments. As the instructor, I participated by writing and reading, just like my students. I opened up the floodgates of writing with this today!!! <br /><br /><br />Thanks to Goldberg I was able to recognize something about myself that I never thought I would come to terms with. I am an "English Professor." I have inspired my students to write. Listening to my students read their work, I heard them profess what I had ignited into them. I had my students forgetting about a 7 am writing class. I had them dwelling within the confines of their soul and providing remnants of their souls to the world through writing. I am excited about using this method with my class at Holmes Community College.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9728018122052966406" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_542851716" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/542851716" />
    <a title="Jade" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10784714-jade"><img alt="Jade" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604586492p2/10784714.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/542851716?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jade" href="/user/show/10784714-jade">Jade</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer542851716" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16001480261099443841">At a time when I was ready to quit writing (yet again), I read <i> Writing Down the Bones </i> and felt revived and excited about writing, something I haven't felt in awhile. Even beyond the helpful advice is the author's energy, the ability to stir up in the reader an excitement for writing because she is excited about it, and it clearly shows. Her words gleam and sing with personality; her writing style is sensitive and down to earth.<br/><br/>While the book heavily emphasizes writing freely in a notebook, I f</span>
  <span id="freeText16001480261099443841" style="display:none">At a time when I was ready to quit writing (yet again), I read <i> Writing Down the Bones </i> and felt revived and excited about writing, something I haven't felt in awhile. Even beyond the helpful advice is the author's energy, the ability to stir up in the reader an excitement for writing because she is excited about it, and it clearly shows. Her words gleam and sing with personality; her writing style is sensitive and down to earth.<br /><br />While the book heavily emphasizes writing freely in a notebook, I found it has a happy compromise about pausing at some point (later on) to "re-envision" what you've written. <i> Writing Down the Bones </i> would most likely appeal more to memoir writers and poets than novelists, but I think anyone can learn some things from it.<br /><br />The interview at the end of the book tackles the idea of the differences between novel writing and other types of writing, which was helpful even if it made me a little nervous!<br /><br />Natalie admits in that interview what a big challenge it was for her to write a novel as she is more of a non-linear (my phrase) writer, but trudged on anyhow. The book does get a bit repetitive at times, but then again, it's good reinforcement. <br /><br />If you're looking for a structured book about how to organize/outline a novel, look elsewhere, such as <i> The Everything Guide to Writing Your First Novel </i> by Hallie Ephron. If you're looking for a way to break out of a writing rut, just get some notebooks filled, and find fresh ways of looking at the world, then this is your book. And if you're greatly disturbed by Zen Buddhist concepts you might want to skip it, or if you can, take her advice for writing and not focus too much on her Buddhism.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16001480261099443841" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Her persona is more a cheerleader than a critical editor, so if your biggest problem is getting started in the first place, this is a great book to read.</span>

<div id="review_2276310583" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer921916284203551828">Another great book about writing to read when I'm procrastinating writing! I listened to an anniversary edition that included the author's updated observations and comments about her initial words. I enjoyed the hindsight as well as Goldberg's Judeo-Buddhist influences on her writing craft.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

  }

In The Right to Write, Julia Cameron\'s most revolutionary book, the author of the bestselling self-help guide The Artist\'s Way, asserts that conventional writing wisdom would have you believe in a false doctrine that stifles creativity. With the techniques and anecdotes in The Right to Write, readers learn to make writing a natural, intensely personal part of life. Wired for Story reveals these cognitive secrets—and it’s a game-changer for anyone who has ever set pen to paper.     The vast majority of writing advice focuses on “writing well” as if it were the same as telling a great story. This is exactly where many aspiring writers fail—they strive for beautiful metaphors, authentic dialogue, and interesting characters, losing sight of the one thing that every engaging story must do: ignite the brain’s hardwired desire to learn what happens next. When writers tap into the evolutionary purpose of story and electrify our curiosity, it triggers a delicious dopamine rush that tells us to pay attention. Without it, even the most perfect prose won’t hold anyone’s interest.     Backed by recent breakthroughs in neuroscience as well as examples from novels, screenplays, and short stories, Wired for Story offers a revolutionary look at story as the brain experiences it. It is now being used as a textbook in classes at University of Minnesota, <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText7452202980980803336\" style=\"display:none\">This updated 2018 Classic Edition contains the original version of William Strunk\'s The Elements of Style, plus a variety of enhancements that make this book even more useful. It is now being used as a textbook in classes at University of Minnesota, University of Texas, UC Berkeley, and elsewhere.  Generations of college students and writers have learned the basics of English grammar from this short book. It was rated &quot;one of the 100 most influential books written in English&quot; by Time in 2011, and iconic author Stephen King recommended it as a grammar primer that all aspiring writers should read.  Written a century ago, Strunk\'s book is a nostalgic link to the Art Deco era and the Roaring Twenties. Many of the grammar rules listed in his book still apply today; but the English language has changed over the years, and some of these rules have are now obsolete. This Classic Edition addresses these changes with the following enhancements and additional content:  1. This 2018 update adds two new chapters requested by college professors and students: Basic Rules of Capitalization and Style Rules for Better Writing.  2. Editor\'s notes have been inserted throughout the book to flag grammar rules that are become obsolete and to provide up-to-date advice for students and writers.  3. Emojis have been added to help readers identify correct examples from errors at a glance.  4. A Study Guide is included in the last chapter, and the paperback version includes blank, lined pages in the back of the book for note taking.  5. The e-book version has been restyled for improved display on the latest generations of digital book-reading devices.  Elements of Style: Classic Edition 2018 gives students and writers a blueprint that they can follow to write clearly and effectively while learning the fundamental rules of English Grammar.  NOTE: Some courses may specify other versions of this book, such as Elements of Style 4th Edition by E.B. White, or Elements of Style 2017, which builds on Strunk\'s work and presents 500+ up-to-date grammar and style rules for students and writers. If your course requires one of these versions, use these links to obtain the correct book:  --The Elements of Style, 4th Edition (Strunk &amp; White) http://amazon.com/dp/020530902X  --Elements of <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15450454179492850462">Natalie Goldberg lived in Brooklyn until she was six, when her family moved out to Farmingdale, Long Island, where her father owned the bar the Aero Tavern. From a young age, Goldberg was mad for books and reading, and especially loved Carson McCullers's <i> The Ballad of the Sad Cafe </i> , which she read in ninth grade. She thinks that single book led her eventually to put pen to paper when she was twe</span>
  <span id="freeText15450454179492850462" style="display:none">Natalie Goldberg lived in Brooklyn until she was six, when her family moved out to Farmingdale, Long Island, where her father owned the bar the Aero Tavern. From a young age, Goldberg was mad for books and reading, and especially loved Carson McCullers's <i> The Ballad of the Sad Cafe </i> , which she read in ninth grade. She thinks that single book led her eventually to put pen to paper when she was twenty-four years old. She received a BA in English literature from George Washington University and an MA in humanities from St. John's University.<br /><br />Goldberg has painted for as long as she has written, and her paintings can be seen in Living Color: A Writer Paints Her World and Top of My Lungs: Poems and Paintings. They can also be viewed at the Ernesto Mayans Gallery on Canyon Road in Sante Fe.<br /><br />A dedicated teacher, Goldberg has taught writing and literature for the last thirty-five years. She also leads national workshops and retreats, and her schedule can be accessed via her website: nataliegoldberg.com<br /><br />In 2006, she completed with the filmmaker Mary Feidt a one-hour documentary, Tangled Up in Bob, about Bob Dylan's childhood on the Iron Range in Northern Minnesota. The film can be obtained on Amazon or the website tangledupinbob.com.<br /><br />Goldberg has been a serious Zen practitioner since 1974 and studied with Katagiri Roshi from 1978 to 1984.<br /></span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/trivia/work/937841-writing-down-the-bones-freeing-the-writer-within">Trivia About Writing Down the ...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
        <div class="mediumText">No trivia or quizzes yet. <a href="/trivia/work/937841-writing-down-the-bones-freeing-the-writer-within">Add some now &raquo;</a></div>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>


      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/937841-writing-down-the-bones-freeing-the-writer-within">Quotes from Writing Down the ...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Write what disturbs you, what you fear, what you have not been willing to speak about. Be willing to be split open.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/13553-write-what-disturbs-you-what-you-fear-what-you-have">630 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;We are important and our lives are important, magnificent really, and their details are worthy to be recorded. This is how writers must think, this is how we must sit down with pen in hand. We were here; we are human beings; this is how we lived. Let it be known, the earth passed before us. Our details are important. Otherwise, if they are not, we can drop a bomb and it doesn't matter. . . Recording the details of our lives is a stance against bombs with their mass ability to kill, against too much speed and efficiency. A writer must say yes to life, to all of life: the water glasses, the Kemp's half-and-half, the ketchup on the counter. It is not a writer's task to say, "It is dumb to live in a small town or to eat in a café when you can eat macrobiotic at home." Our task is to say a holy yes to the real things of our life as they exist – the real truth of who we are: several pounds overweight, the gray, cold street outside, the Christmas tinsel in the showcase, the Jewish writer in the orange booth across from her blond friend who has black children. We must become writers who accept things as they are, come to love the details, and step forward with a yes on our lips so there can be no more noes in the world, noes that invalidate life and stop these details from continuing.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/48088-we-are-important-and-our-lives-are-important-magnificent-really">169 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right" href="/work/quotes/937841-writing-down-the-bones-freeing-the-writer-within">More quotes&hellip;</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
